     <p>The <b>University of Utah</b> (also referred to as <b>the U</b>, <b>the U of U</b>, or <b>Utah</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/Public_university" title="Public university">public</a> <a href="/wiki/Mixed-sex_education" title="Mixed-sex education">coeducational</a> <a href="/wiki/Space_grant_colleges" title="Space grant colleges" class="mw-redirect">space-grant</a> <a href="/wiki/Research_university" title="Research university" class="mw-redirect">research university</a> in <a href="/wiki/Salt_Lake_City" title="Salt Lake City">Salt Lake City</a>, <a href="/wiki/Utah" title="Utah">Utah</a>, United States. As the state's <a href="/wiki/Flagship_university" title="Flagship university" class="mw-redirect">flagship university</a>, the university offers more than 100 undergraduate majors and more than 90 graduate degree programs.<sup id="cite_ref-fast_facts_5-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fast_facts-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> Graduate studies include the <a href="/wiki/S.J._Quinney_College_of_Law" title="S.J. Quinney College of Law">S.J. Quinney College of Law</a> and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Utah_School_of_Medicine" title="University of Utah School of Medicine">School of Medicine</a>, Utah's only <a href="/wiki/Medical_school" title="Medical school">medical school</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-aamc_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aamc-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> As of Autumn 2012, there are 24,840 <a href="/wiki/Undergraduate_education" title="Undergraduate education">undergraduate</a> students and 7,548 <a href="/wiki/Postgraduate_education" title="Postgraduate education">graduate</a> students, for an enrollment total of 32,388; with 83% coming from Utah and 9% coming from foreign countries.<sup id="cite_ref-fast_facts_5-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fast_facts-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> Just over 10% of students live on campus.<sup id="cite_ref-plan_elements_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-plan_elements-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university's athletic teams, the <a href="/wiki/Utah_Utes" title="Utah Utes">Utes</a>, participate in <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">NCAA</a> <a href="/wiki/Division_I_(NCAA)" title="Division I (NCAA)">Division I</a> athletics (<a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I_FBS_National_Football_Championship" title="NCAA Division I FBS National Football Championship" class="mw-redirect">FBS</a> for football) as a member of the <a href="/wiki/Pacific-12_Conference" title="Pacific-12 Conference">Pacific-12 Conference</a>. Its football team has received national attention in recent years for winning the <a href="/wiki/2005_Fiesta_Bowl" title="2005 Fiesta Bowl">2005 Fiesta Bowl</a><sup id="cite_ref-fiesta_bowl_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fiesta_bowl-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/2009_Sugar_Bowl" title="2009 Sugar Bowl">2009 Sugar Bowl</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-sugar_bowl_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sugar_bowl-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university was established in 1850 as the <b>University of Deseret</b> by the General Assembly of the provisional <a href="/wiki/State_of_Deseret" title="State of Deseret">State of Deseret</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-sesquicentennial_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sesquicentennial-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup> making it Utah's oldest institution of higher education.<sup id="cite_ref-fast_facts_5-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fast_facts-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> It received its current name in 1892, four years before Utah attained statehood, and moved to its current location in 1900.<sup id="cite_ref-sesquicentennial_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sesquicentennial-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

            <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-14"><a href="#Gymnastics"><span class="tocnumber">5.3</span> <span class="toctext">Gymnastics</span></a></li> 
            <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-15"><a href="#Marching_band"><span class="tocnumber">5.4</span> <span class="toctext">Marching band</span></a></li> 
           </ul> </li> 
          <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-16"><a href="#Student_life"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Student life</span></a></li>

     </table> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Utah&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:MountVanCott.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/MountVanCott.JPG/220px-MountVanCott.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/MountVanCott.JPG/330px-MountVanCott.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/MountVanCott.JPG/440px-MountVanCott.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:MountVanCott.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The 
        <a href="/wiki/Block_U" title="Block U">Block U</a> has overlooked the university since 1907
        <sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>A Board of Regents was organized by <a href="/wiki/Brigham_Young" title="Brigham Young">Brigham Young</a> to establish a university in the Salt Lake Valley.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> The university was established on February 28, 1850, as the <i>University of Deseret</i> by the General Assembly of the provisional <a href="/wiki/State_of_Deseret" title="State of Deseret">State of Deseret</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Orson_Spencer" title="Orson Spencer">Orson Spencer</a> was appointed as the first chancellor of the university. Early classes were held in private homes or wherever space could be found. The university closed in 1853 due to lack of funds and lack of <a href="/wiki/Feeder_school" title="Feeder school">feeder schools</a>.</p> 
     <p>Following years of intermittent classes in the Salt Lake City <a href="/wiki/Council_House_(Salt_Lake_City)" title="Council House (Salt Lake City)">Council House</a>, the university began to be reestablished in 1867 under the direction of <a href="/wiki/David_O._Calder" title="David O. Calder">David O. Calder</a>, who was followed by <a href="/wiki/John_R._Park" title="John R. Park">John R. Park</a> in 1869. The university moved out of the council house into the Union Academy building in 1876 and into Union Square in 1884. In 1892, the school's name was changed to the University of Utah, and <a href="/wiki/John_R._Park" title="John R. Park">John R. Park</a> began arranging to obtain land belonging to the U.S. Army's <a href="/wiki/Fort_Douglas_(Utah)" title="Fort Douglas (Utah)" class="mw-redirect">Fort Douglas</a> on the east bench of the <a href="/wiki/Salt_Lake_Valley" title="Salt Lake Valley">Salt Lake Valley</a>, where the university moved permanently in 1900. Additional <a href="/wiki/Fort_Douglas_(Utah)" title="Fort Douglas (Utah)" class="mw-redirect">Fort Douglas</a> land has been granted to the university over the years, and the fort was officially closed on October 26, 1991.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> Upon his death in 1900, Dr. John R. Park bequeathed his entire fortune to the university.<sup id="cite_ref-sesquicentennial_1-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sesquicentennial-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-history_of_utah_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history_of_utah-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:UofU_campus_close-up_early_1920s.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/UofU_campus_close-up_early_1920s.jpg/220px-UofU_campus_close-up_early_1920s.jpg" width="220" height="106" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/UofU_campus_close-up_early_1920s.jpg/330px-UofU_campus_close-up_early_1920s.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/UofU_campus_close-up_early_1920s.jpg/440px-UofU_campus_close-up_early_1920s.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:UofU_campus_close-up_early_1920s.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The University of Utah campus in the early 1920s
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The university grew rapidly in the early 20th century but was involved in an <a href="/wiki/Academic_freedom" title="Academic freedom">academic freedom</a> controversy in 1915 when <a href="/wiki/Joseph_T._Kingsbury" title="Joseph T. Kingsbury">Joseph T. Kingsbury</a> recommended that five faculty members be dismissed after a graduation speaker made a speech critical of mayor <a href="/wiki/William_Spry" title="William Spry">William Spry</a>. One third of the faculty resigned in protest of these dismissals. Some felt that the dismissals were a result of the <a href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints" title="The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">LDS Church</a>'s influence on the university, while others felt that they reflected a more general pattern of repressing religious and political expression that might be deemed offensive. The controversy was largely resolved when Kingsbury resigned in 1916, but university operations were again interrupted by World War I, and later <a href="/wiki/The_Great_Depression" title="The Great Depression" class="mw-redirect">The Great Depression</a> and World War II. Student enrollment dropped to a low of 3,418 during the last year of World War II, but <a href="/wiki/A._Ray_Olpin" title="A. Ray Olpin">A. Ray Olpin</a> was able to make substantial additions to campus following the war, and enrollment reached 12,000 by the time he retired in 1964. Growth continued throughout the following decades as the university developed into a center for computer, medical, and other research.<sup id="cite_ref-sesquicentennial_1-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sesquicentennial-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-transition_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-transition-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>During the <a href="/wiki/2002_Winter_Olympics" title="2002 Winter Olympics">2002 Winter Olympics</a>, the university hosted the Olympic Village,<sup id="cite_ref-olympic_village_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-olympic_village-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> a housing complex for the Olympic and Paralympic athletes, as well as the opening and closing ceremonies.<sup id="cite_ref-olympic_stadium_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-olympic_stadium-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> Prior to the events, the university received a facelift that included extensive renovations to the <a href="/wiki/Rice%E2%80%93Eccles_Stadium" title="Rice?Eccles Stadium" class="mw-redirect">Rice?Eccles Stadium</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-olympic_stadium_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-olympic_stadium-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> a <a href="/wiki/Light_rail" title="Light rail">light rail</a> track leading to downtown Salt Lake City,<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> a new student center known as the Heritage Center,<sup id="cite_ref-olympic_village_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-olympic_village-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> an array of new student housing,<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> and what is now a 180-room campus hotel and conference center.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Campus">Campus</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Utah&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Campus">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Uofu_walkwaywithbuildings.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Uofu_walkwaywithbuildings.jpg/220px-Uofu_walkwaywithbuildings.jpg" width="220" height="158" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Uofu_walkwaywithbuildings.jpg/330px-Uofu_walkwaywithbuildings.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Uofu_walkwaywithbuildings.jpg/440px-Uofu_walkwaywithbuildings.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Uofu_walkwaywithbuildings.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> A view of lower campus
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Campus takes up 1,534 acres (6.21&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup>), including the Health Sciences complex, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Utah_Research_Park" title="University of Utah Research Park">Research Park</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Fort_Douglas,_Utah" title="Fort Douglas, Utah" class="mw-redirect">Fort Douglas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-inventory_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-inventory-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> It is located on the east bench of the <a href="/wiki/Salt_Lake_Valley" title="Salt Lake Valley">Salt Lake Valley</a>, close to the <a href="/wiki/Wasatch_Range" title="Wasatch Range">Wasatch Range</a> and approximately 2 miles east of <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Salt_Lake_City" title="Downtown Salt Lake City">downtown Salt Lake City</a>.</p> 
     <p>Most courses take place on the west side of campus, known as lower campus due to its lower elevation. <a href="/wiki/University_of_Utah_Circle" title="University of Utah Circle">Presidents Circle</a> is a loop of buildings named after past university presidents with a courtyard in the center. Major libraries on lower campus include the <a href="/wiki/J._Willard_Marriott_Library" title="J. Willard Marriott Library">J. Willard Marriott Library</a> and the <a href="/wiki/S.J._Quinney_College_of_Law#Law_library" title="S.J. Quinney College of Law">S.J. Quinney Law Library</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-inventory_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-inventory-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> The primary <a href="/wiki/Student_activity_center" title="Student activity center">student activity center</a> is the <a href="/wiki/A._Ray_Olpin" title="A. Ray Olpin">A. Ray Olpin</a> University Union, and campus fitness centers include the Health, Physical Education, and Recreation Complex (HPER) and the <a href="/wiki/Nielsen_Fieldhouse" title="Nielsen Fieldhouse">Nielsen Fieldhouse</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-inventory_6-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-inventory-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Kingsbury_Hall.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Kingsbury_Hall.jpg/220px-Kingsbury_Hall.jpg" width="220" height="115" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Kingsbury_Hall.jpg/330px-Kingsbury_Hall.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Kingsbury_Hall.jpg/440px-Kingsbury_Hall.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Kingsbury_Hall.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Kingsbury_Hall" title="Kingsbury Hall">Kingsbury Hall</a> at the 
        <a href="/wiki/Presidents_Circle" title="Presidents Circle" class="mw-redirect">Presidents Circle</a> is a center for the performing arts
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Lower campus is also home to most public venues, such as the <a href="/wiki/Rice%E2%80%93Eccles_Stadium" title="Rice?Eccles Stadium" class="mw-redirect">Rice?Eccles Stadium</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Jon_M._Huntsman_Center" title="Jon M. Huntsman Center">Jon M. Huntsman Center</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Utah_Museum_of_Natural_History" title="Utah Museum of Natural History" class="mw-redirect">Utah Museum of Natural History</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Utah_Museum_of_Fine_Arts" title="Utah Museum of Fine Arts">Utah Museum of Fine Arts</a>, a museum with rotating exhibitions and a permanent collection of American, European, African, and Asian art. Venues for performing arts include <a href="/wiki/Kingsbury_Hall" title="Kingsbury Hall">Kingsbury Hall</a>, used for touring companies and concerts, Pioneer Memorial Theatre, used by the professional <a href="/wiki/Pioneer_Theatre_Company" title="Pioneer Theatre Company">Pioneer Theatre Company</a>, David P. Gardner Hall, used by the School of Music and for musical performances, and the Marriott Center for Dance. <a href="/wiki/Red_Butte_Garden_and_Arboretum" title="Red Butte Garden and Arboretum">Red Butte Garden</a>, with formal gardens and natural areas, is located on the far east side of campus.<sup id="cite_ref-cultural_venues_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cultural_venues-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:University_of_Utah_Hospital_in_2009.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e1/University_of_Utah_Hospital_in_2009.JPG/220px-University_of_Utah_Hospital_in_2009.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e1/University_of_Utah_Hospital_in_2009.JPG/330px-University_of_Utah_Hospital_in_2009.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e1/University_of_Utah_Hospital_in_2009.JPG/440px-University_of_Utah_Hospital_in_2009.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:University_of_Utah_Hospital_in_2009.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The 
        <a href="/wiki/University_of_Utah_Medical_Center" title="University of Utah Medical Center" class="mw-redirect">University of Utah Medical Center</a>
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The health sciences complex, at the northeast end of campus, includes the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Utah_Medical_Center" title="University of Utah Medical Center" class="mw-redirect">University of Utah Medical Center</a>, <a href="/wiki/Primary_Children%27s_Medical_Center" title="Primary Children's Medical Center">Primary Children's Medical Center</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Huntsman_Cancer_Institute" title="Huntsman Cancer Institute">Huntsman Cancer Institute</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Moran_Eye_Center" title="Moran Eye Center">Moran Eye Center</a>, and the Spencer Eccles Health Sciences Library.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> South of the health sciences complex, several university residence halls and apartments are clustered together near <a href="/wiki/Fort_Douglas,_Utah" title="Fort Douglas, Utah" class="mw-redirect">Fort Douglas</a> and the Heritage Center, which serves as a student center and cafeteria for this area.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> In addition, there are 1,115 university apartments for students, staff, and faculty across three apartment complexes on campus.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup> At the southeast end of campus is <a href="/wiki/University_of_Utah_Research_Park" title="University of Utah Research Park">Research Park</a>, which is home to research companies including <a href="/wiki/ARUP_Laboratories" title="ARUP Laboratories">ARUP Laboratories</a>, <a href="/wiki/Evans_%26_Sutherland" title="Evans &amp; Sutherland">Evans &amp; Sutherland</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sarcos" title="Sarcos">Sarcos</a>, <a href="/wiki/Idaho_Technology" title="Idaho Technology">Idaho Technology</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Myriad_Genetics" title="Myriad Genetics">Myriad Genetics</a>.</p> 
     <p>Courses are also held at off-campus centers located in <a href="/wiki/Bountiful,_Utah" title="Bountiful, Utah">Bountiful</a>, <a href="/wiki/Murray,_Utah" title="Murray, Utah">Murray</a>, <a href="/wiki/Park_City,_Utah" title="Park City, Utah">Park City</a>, downtown <a href="/wiki/Salt_Lake_City" title="Salt Lake City">Salt Lake City</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sandy,_Utah" title="Sandy, Utah">Sandy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_housing">Student housing</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Utah&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Student housing">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The University of Utah provides student housing in an 32-building housing complex on campus. The complex consists of 7 housing areas: Chapel Glen, Gateway Heights, Sage Point, Officer's Circle, Benchmark Plaza, Shoreline Ridge, and the Donna Garff Marriott Honors Residential Scholars Community. The new Donna Garff Marriott Honors Residential Scholars Community, a dormitory for honors students, was completed Fall 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Utah&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:UTA_TRAX_-_From_SLC_to_Sandy_on_South_Temple_street_-_February_2011.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/UTA_TRAX_-_From_SLC_to_Sandy_on_South_Temple_street_-_February_2011.jpg/220px-UTA_TRAX_-_From_SLC_to_Sandy_on_South_Temple_street_-_February_2011.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/UTA_TRAX_-_From_SLC_to_Sandy_on_South_Temple_street_-_February_2011.jpg/330px-UTA_TRAX_-_From_SLC_to_Sandy_on_South_Temple_street_-_February_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/UTA_TRAX_-_From_SLC_to_Sandy_on_South_Temple_street_-_February_2011.jpg/440px-UTA_TRAX_-_From_SLC_to_Sandy_on_South_Temple_street_-_February_2011.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:UTA_TRAX_-_From_SLC_to_Sandy_on_South_Temple_street_-_February_2011.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/TRAX_(light_rail)" title="TRAX (light rail)">UTA TRAX</a> services the university and other parts of Salt Lake City
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>A number of campus shuttles, running on biodiesel and used vegetable oil,<sup id="cite_ref-sei2009_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sei2009-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup> circle the campus on six different routes.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Utah_Transit_Authority" title="Utah Transit Authority">Utah Transit Authority</a> (UTA) runs several buses through the university area as well as the <a href="/wiki/TRAX_(light_rail)" title="TRAX (light rail)">TRAX</a> <a href="/wiki/Red_Line_(TRAX)" title="Red Line (TRAX)">Red Line</a> (<a href="/wiki/Light_rail" title="Light rail">light rail</a>), which runs to <a href="/wiki/Daybreak_Parkway_(UTA_station)" title="Daybreak Parkway (UTA station)">South Jordan</a>. Riders can travel downtown, to <i><a href="/wiki/FrontRunner" title="FrontRunner">FrontRunner</a></i> (<a href="/wiki/Commuter_rail_in_North_America" title="Commuter rail in North America">commuter rail</a>), to <a href="/wiki/West_Valley_City,_Utah" title="West Valley City, Utah">West Valley</a>, to the <a href="/wiki/Salt_Lake_City_International_Airport" title="Salt Lake City International Airport">Salt Lake City International Airport</a>, or to <a href="/wiki/Sandy,_Utah" title="Sandy, Utah">Sandy</a> by transferring to the TRAX <a href="/wiki/Green_Line_(TRAX)" title="Green Line (TRAX)">Green</a> or <a href="/wiki/Blue_Line_(TRAX)" title="Blue Line (TRAX)">Blue</a> lines. Students and staff can use their university IDs to ride UTA buses, TRAX, and <i>FrontRunner</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The University has recently unveiled a new plan for a friendlier campus for bicyclers called the &quot;Bicycle Master Plan&quot; which aims to transform the campus into a safer and more accessible place for bicyclers and to promote the increase of bicycle ridership. The plan emphasizes both campus pathways and on-street facilities that connect the core campus area with surrounding neighborhoods. The Bicycle Master Plan gives guidelines for facilities and programs that are within the University?s jurisdiction. It also provides recommendations for the University to work with external entities such as UDOT, UTA, and Salt Lake City to improve bicycling conditions in locations that are important to the campus environment, but which are not under the University?s direct control.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sustainability">Sustainability</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Utah&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Sustainability">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The university is ranked 3rd by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Environmental_Protection_Agency" title="United States Environmental Protection Agency">EPA</a> for annual <a href="/wiki/Green_energy" title="Green energy" class="mw-redirect">green power</a> usage among universities, with 31% of its power coming from <a href="/wiki/Wind_power" title="Wind power">wind</a> and <a href="/wiki/Solar_power" title="Solar power">solar</a> sources.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> Other sustainability efforts include a permanent sustainability office, a campus <a href="/wiki/Cogeneration" title="Cogeneration">cogeneration</a> plant, building upgrades and energy efficient building standards, behavior modification programs, purchasing local <a href="/wiki/Produce" title="Produce">produce</a>, and student groups including a bicycle collective.<sup id="cite_ref-sei2009_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sei2009-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup> Sustainability and transportation are also a large part of the university's campus master plan.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> The Sustainable Endowments Institute gave the university a &quot;B+&quot; in its College Sustainability Report Card 2011, with A's for climate change and energy, food and recycling, student involvement, and transportation.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The expanded recycling program launched on July 1, 2007. Since its launch, the program has continued to grow and refine its procedures to better accommodate a growing campus' needs. Currently there are programs in place for paper, cardboard, aluminum, batteries, printer cartridges, wooden pallets and plastics #1 and #2.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Renewable_energy">Renewable energy</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Utah&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Renewable energy">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>On July 7, 2011 the university unveiled its plans to be the first location in the United States to install solar ivy. Unlike rooftop panels, solar ivy panels are small and shaped like ivy so that they can be installed in an attractive arrangement that will scale walls, much like ivy growing over a building?s surface. These panels were designed by Sustainably Minded Interactive Technology of New York.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>A renewable energy partnership was entered into by the university, Rocky Mountain Power and 3Degrees on September 28, 2011 allowing the purchase of renewable wind power that in its first year will produce 98,233,000 kilowatt-hours of wind energy, which is 36%<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> of the university's total power usage, with plans for an additional two-year renewable energy commitment. The university?s first-year renewable energy purchase through Blue Sky and 3Degrees has the combined environmental benefit of taking more than 13,200 cars off the road for one year or planting 1.7 million trees. The university?s support for renewable energy is made possible through a student fee-funded sustainability program established in 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university unveiled the addition of a new solar array system on April 16, 2012 on the rooftop of the Museum of Natural History. This is the second system installed on the university's campus, the other being at the HPER East building. The Natural History Museum of Utah?s system is a 330-kilowatt system, while the HPER East system is a 263-kilowatt system. The combined arrays consist of 2,470 Sharp photovoltaic panels covering 40,000 square feet of rooftop space and together they will annually produce 802,240 kilowatt hours<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Organization">Organization</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Utah&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Organization">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:The_Park_Building_at_the_University_of_Utah.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/The_Park_Building_at_the_University_of_Utah.jpg/220px-The_Park_Building_at_the_University_of_Utah.jpg" width="220" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/The_Park_Building_at_the_University_of_Utah.jpg/330px-The_Park_Building_at_the_University_of_Utah.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/The_Park_Building_at_the_University_of_Utah.jpg/440px-The_Park_Building_at_the_University_of_Utah.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:The_Park_Building_at_the_University_of_Utah.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The Park Building is the center of university administration
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The university is part of the <a href="/wiki/Utah_System_of_Higher_Education" title="Utah System of Higher Education">Utah System of Higher Education</a>. As of 2009, the university's endowment is US$668 million.<sup id="cite_ref-nacubo_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nacubo-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> The colleges at the university are:</p> 
     <table> 
      <tbody>
       <tr> 
        <td> 
         <ul> 
          <li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Utah_College_of_Architecture_and_Planning" title="University of Utah College of Architecture and Planning">College of Architecture + Planning</a></li> 
          <li>College of Dentistry</li> 
          <li>College of Education</li> 
          <li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Utah_College_of_Engineering" title="University of Utah College of Engineering">College of Engineering</a></li> 
          <li>College of Fine Arts</li> 
          <li>College of Health</li> 
          <li>College of Humanities</li> 
          <li>College of Mines &amp; Earth Sciences</li> 
          <li>College of Nursing</li> 
          <li>College of Pharmacy</li> 
         </ul> </td> 
        <td width="20"></td> 
        <td style="vertical-align:top;"> 
         <ul> 
          <li>College of Science</li> 
          <li>College of Social &amp; Behavioral Science</li> 
          <li>College of Social Work</li> 
          <li>Continuing Education</li> 
          <li><a href="/wiki/David_Eccles_School_of_Business" title="David Eccles School of Business">David Eccles School of Business</a></li> 
          <li>Graduate School</li> 
          <li>Honors College</li> 
          <li>Office of Undergraduate Studies</li> 
          <li><a href="/wiki/S.J._Quinney_College_of_Law" title="S.J. Quinney College of Law">S.J. Quinney College of Law</a></li> 
          <li><a href="/wiki/University_of_Utah_School_of_Medicine" title="University of Utah School of Medicine">School of Medicine</a></li> 
         </ul> </td> 
       </tr> 
      </tbody>
     </table> 
     <p>In addition to the departments in these colleges, there are a number of interdisciplinary academic programs.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Academics">Academics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Utah&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Academics">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <table class="infobox vcard" style="width: 22em"> 
      <tbody>
       <tr>
