       </tr> 
       <tr> 
        <th><i><a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">Times</a></i><sup id="cite_ref-Rankings_THES_W_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rankings_THES_W-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup></th> 
        <td>134</td> 
       </tr> 
      </tbody>
     </table> 
     <p>The university offers 72 undergraduate majors, more than 70 minors and certificates, more than 40 teaching majors and minors, and 95 major fields of study at the graduate level.<sup id="cite_ref-academic_programs_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-academic_programs-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup> Students at the undergraduate level can also create an individualized major under the direction of the Bachelor of University Studies program and the supervision of a <a href="/wiki/Tenure" title="Tenure" class="mw-redirect">tenure-track</a> faculty member.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup> The university has three semesters a year: spring, summer, and fall.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup> Undergraduate tuition and fees for 2012?2013 were US$3,008 for Utah residents and $9,485 for non-residents per 12-credit-hour semester.<sup id="cite_ref-fast_facts_5-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fast_facts-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university is classified as a research university with very high research activity by the <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Foundation_for_the_Advancement_of_Teaching" title="Carnegie Foundation for the Advancement of Teaching">Carnegie Foundation</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-carnegie_classification_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-carnegie_classification-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup> with research and training awards for 2010-2011 amounting to US$410,563,908.<sup id="cite_ref-fast_facts_5-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fast_facts-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> The university's research expenditures were the 67th highest in the nation in the <a href="/wiki/Center_for_Measuring_University_Performance" title="Center for Measuring University Performance">Center for Measuring University Performance</a>'s 2008 report. Additionally, the university was the 58th highest for federal research expenditures, 52nd for <a href="/wiki/United_States_National_Academy_of_Sciences" title="United States National Academy of Sciences" class="mw-redirect">National Academy of Sciences</a> membership, 50th for faculty awards, 51st for doctorates awarded, and 42nd for <a href="/wiki/Postdoctoral_research" title="Postdoctoral research">postdoctoral</a> appointees.<sup id="cite_ref-cmup_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cmup-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2009, the University of Utah created the highest number of startup companies in the nation based on university technology, just ahead of <a href="/wiki/MIT" title="MIT" class="mw-redirect">MIT</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Admissions_and_demographics">Admissions and demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Utah&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Admissions and demographics">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>In 2007?2008, the university accepted 94% and admitted 80% of its 16,200 domestic undegraduate applicants; accepted 94% and admitted 66% of its 1,017 international undergraduate applicants; accepted 80% and admitted 44% of its 6,773 domestic graduate applicants; and accepted 70% and admitted 38% of its 1,992 international graduate applicants.<sup id="cite_ref-admission_report_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-admission_report-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Of admitted freshmen, the average <a href="/wiki/Grade_(education)#United_States" title="Grade (education)" class="mw-redirect">GPA</a> was 3.4 and the average <a href="/wiki/ACT_(test)" title="ACT (test)">ACT</a> score was 23.5.<sup id="cite_ref-admission_report_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-admission_report-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup> The university uses an admissions index number that gives equal weight to GPA and ACT/<a href="/wiki/SAT" title="SAT">SAT</a> scores. If a freshman applicant's index number is at or above the current cutoff, they are guaranteed admission, assuming the student has or will graduate from an accredited high school, has satisfactorily completed all course requirements, has a cumulative high school GPA of at least 2.6, and has an ACT score of at least 18 or SAT score of at least 860. Special requirements apply to non-accredited high schools.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In 2010, the undergraduate and graduate student body was 30,819, with 23,371 <a href="/wiki/Undergraduate_education" title="Undergraduate education">undergraduate</a> students and 7,448 <a href="/wiki/Postgraduate_education" title="Postgraduate education">graduate</a> students. 71% of students were full-time, 56% were male and 44% female, 84% were Utah residents, and 6% were foreign students.<sup id="cite_ref-fast_facts_5-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fast_facts-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> The student body was 77% white, 6% non-resident alien, 5% Asian, Native Hawaiian, or Pacific Islander, 5% Hispanic, 1% black, and 1% Native American. Ethnicity or citizenship was unknown for 6% of the student body.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup> The university was ranked 20th by <a href="/wiki/The_Princeton_Review" title="The Princeton Review">The Princeton Review</a> for having the most religious students in the nation in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_programs">Notable programs</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Utah&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Notable programs">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Carlson_Hall_University_of_Utah.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Carlson_Hall_University_of_Utah.jpeg/220px-Carlson_Hall_University_of_Utah.jpeg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Carlson_Hall_University_of_Utah.jpeg/330px-Carlson_Hall_University_of_Utah.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Carlson_Hall_University_of_Utah.jpeg/440px-Carlson_Hall_University_of_Utah.jpeg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Carlson_Hall_University_of_Utah.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Carlson Hall hosts a number of different offices, including some for the S.J. Quinney College of Law
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The University of Utah has the only accredited architecture program in Utah,<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup> as well as the only <a href="/wiki/Medical_school" title="Medical school">medical school</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-aamc_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aamc-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> The medical school has made several notable contributions to medicine, such as establishing the first <a href="/wiki/Cerebrovascular_disease" title="Cerebrovascular disease">Cerebrovascular Disease</a> Unit west of the <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_River" title="Mississippi River">Mississippi River</a> in 1970 and administering the world's first permanent artificial heart, the <a href="/wiki/Jarvik-7" title="Jarvik-7" class="mw-redirect">Jarvik-7</a>, to <a href="/wiki/Barney_Clark_(patient)" title="Barney Clark (patient)" class="mw-redirect">Barney Clark</a> in 1982.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Uofu_warnockside.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Uofu_warnockside.jpg/170px-Uofu_warnockside.jpg" width="170" height="204" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Uofu_warnockside.jpg/255px-Uofu_warnockside.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Uofu_warnockside.jpg/340px-Uofu_warnockside.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Uofu_warnockside.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The Warnock Engineering Building
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/S.J._Quinney_College_of_Law" title="S.J. Quinney College of Law">S.J. Quinney College of Law</a>, founded in 1913,<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup> was the only <a href="/wiki/Law_school" title="Law school">law school</a> in Utah until the 1970s.</p> 
     <p>The University of Utah was one of the original four nodes of <a href="/wiki/ARPANET#Initial_ARPANET_deployment" title="ARPANET">ARPANET</a>, the world's first <a href="/wiki/Packet-switching" title="Packet-switching" class="mw-redirect">packet-switching</a> computer network and embryo of the current worldwide Internet.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup> Notable innovations of engineering faculty and alumni include the first method for representing surface textures in graphical images, the <a href="/wiki/Gouraud_shading" title="Gouraud shading">Gouraud shading</a> model, magnetic ink printing technology, the Johnson counter <a href="/wiki/Logic_circuit" title="Logic circuit" class="mw-redirect">logic circuit</a>, the oldest algebraic mathematics package still in use (<a href="/wiki/REDUCE" title="REDUCE" class="mw-redirect">REDUCE</a>), the <a href="/wiki/Phong_reflection_model" title="Phong reflection model">Phong reflection model</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Phong_shading" title="Phong shading">Phong shading</a> method, and the <a href="/wiki/Rendering_equation" title="Rendering equation">rendering equation</a>. The school has pioneered work in <a href="/wiki/Asynchronous_circuit" title="Asynchronous circuit">asynchronous circuits</a>, <a href="/wiki/Computer_animation" title="Computer animation">computer animation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Computer_art" title="Computer art">computer art</a>, digital <a href="/wiki/Sound_recording_and_reproduction" title="Sound recording and reproduction">music recording</a>, <a href="/wiki/Graphical_user_interface" title="Graphical user interface">graphical user interfaces</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Stack_machine" title="Stack machine">stack machine</a> architectures.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> The School of Computing also takes part in the <a href="/wiki/Scientific_Computing_and_Imaging_Institute" title="Scientific Computing and Imaging Institute">Scientific Computing and Imaging Institute</a>, which continues to make advances in visualization, scientific computing, and image analysis.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The university has made unique contributions to the study of <a href="/wiki/Genetics" title="Genetics">genetics</a> due in part to long-term <a href="/wiki/Genealogy" title="Genealogy">genealogy</a> efforts of the <a href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints" title="The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">LDS Church</a>, which has allowed researchers to trace genetic disorders through several generations. The relative homogeneity of Utah's population also makes it an ideal laboratory for studies of population genetics.<sup id="cite_ref-genetics_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-genetics-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup> The university is home to the Genetic Science Learning Center, a resource which educates the public about genetics through its website.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In March 2012, the university received unanimous approval from the board of trustees to create a new academic college, the College of Dentistry, which is the university's first new college in sixty years.<sup id="cite_ref-dailyutahchronicle.com_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dailyutahchronicle.com-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> The new college has received funding for a new structure and has started as a debt-free program.<sup id="cite_ref-dailyutahchronicle.com_75-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dailyutahchronicle.com-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> The new school will start enrolling students for the fall semester of 2013 and is expected to average the same cost as the university's medical school tuition.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In August 2012, the University of Utah announced plans to close its <a href="/wiki/Center_for_American_Indian_Languages" title="Center for American Indian Languages">Center for American Indian Languages</a>, which has been home to linguists such as <a href="/wiki/Lyle_Campbell" title="Lyle Campbell">Lyle Campbell</a> and Wick Miller. &quot;The College of Humanities instead will concentrate language-preservation efforts on Utah's tribal tongues,&quot; according to one article.<sup id="cite_ref-republic_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-republic-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup> This closure, said to be for purposes focusing efforts on the language of Utah tribes, &quot;has shocked many in the <a href="/wiki/Language_documentation" title="Language documentation">language conservation</a> world.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup> Linguists, including <a href="/wiki/Ives_Goddard" title="Ives Goddard">Ives Goddard</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Smithsonian_Institution" title="Smithsonian Institution">Smithsonian</a> have expressed serious concern about the negative impact on efforts to preserve indigenous languages throughout the Americas.<sup id="cite_ref-republic_77-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-republic-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletics">Athletics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Utah&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Athletics">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Uofu_huntsmancenter.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Uofu_huntsmancenter.jpg/220px-Uofu_huntsmancenter.jpg" width="220" height="156" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Uofu_huntsmancenter.jpg/330px-Uofu_huntsmancenter.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Uofu_huntsmancenter.jpg/440px-Uofu_huntsmancenter.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Uofu_huntsmancenter.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Jon_M._Huntsman_Center" title="Jon M. Huntsman Center">Jon M. Huntsman Center</a> serves as a basketball and gymnastics venue
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Utah_Utes" title="Utah Utes">Utah Utes</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The university has 7 men's and 11 women's varsity teams.<sup id="cite_ref-athletics_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-athletics-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> Athletic teams include men's baseball, basketball, football, golf, skiing, swimming/diving, and tennis and women's basketball, cross country, gymnastics, skiing, soccer, softball, swimming/diving, tennis, track and field, and volleyball.<sup id="cite_ref-utah_utes_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-utah_utes-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup> The school's sports teams are called the <a href="/wiki/Ute_tribe" title="Ute tribe" class="mw-redirect">Utes</a>, though some teams have an additional nickname, such as &quot;Runnin' Utes&quot; for the men's basketball team.<sup id="cite_ref-basketball_media_guide_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-basketball_media_guide-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> The university participates in the <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">NCAA</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Division_I_(NCAA)" title="Division I (NCAA)">Division I</a> (<a href="/wiki/NCAA_Division_I_FBS_National_Football_Championship" title="NCAA Division I FBS National Football Championship" class="mw-redirect">FBS</a> for football) as part of the <a href="/wiki/Pacific-12_Conference" title="Pacific-12 Conference">Pac-12 Conference</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> There is a fierce <a href="/wiki/Utah%E2%80%93BYU_rivalry" title="Utah?BYU rivalry">Utah?BYU rivalry</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Holy_War_(Utah_vs._BYU)" title="Holy War (Utah vs. BYU)">Utah?BYU football game</a>, traditionally a season finale, has been called the &quot;Holy War&quot; by national broadcasting commentators.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup> The university <a href="/wiki/Fight_song" title="Fight song">fight song</a> is <a href="/wiki/Utah_Utes#Fight_song" title="Utah Utes">&quot;Utah Man&quot;</a>, commonly played at athletic games and other university events.<sup id="cite_ref-ute_traditions_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ute_traditions-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1996, <a href="/wiki/Utah_Utes#Mascot" title="Utah Utes">Swoop</a> was introduced as the new mascot of the University of Utah. Because of relationships with the local Ute Indians, Utah adopted a new mascot. While still known as the Utes, Utah is now represented by the <a href="/wiki/Red-tailed_Hawk" title="Red-tailed Hawk">Red-tailed Hawk</a> known for the use of his tail feathers in Ute head-dresses, and said he &quot;Reflects the soaring spirit of our state and school&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-Utah_Mascot_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Utah_Mascot-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In 2002, the university was one of 20 schools to make the <i><a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News &amp; World Report</a></i> College Sports Honor Roll.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2005, Utah became the first school to produce No. 1 overall draft picks in both the <a href="/wiki/NFL_Draft" title="NFL Draft" class="mw-redirect">NFL Draft</a> and <a href="/wiki/NBA_Draft" title="NBA Draft" class="mw-redirect">NBA Draft</a> for the same year.<sup id="cite_ref-bogut_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bogut-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Alex_Smith" title="Alex Smith">Alex Smith</a> was picked first overall by the <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_49ers" title="San Francisco 49ers">San Francisco 49ers</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2005_NFL_Draft" title="2005 NFL Draft">2005 NFL Draft</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Bogut" title="Andrew Bogut">Andrew Bogut</a> was picked first overall by the <a href="/wiki/Milwaukee_Bucks" title="Milwaukee Bucks">Milwaukee Bucks</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2005_NBA_Draft" title="2005 NBA Draft" class="mw-redirect">2005 NBA Draft</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup> The university has won ten <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Skiing_Championships" title="NCAA Skiing Championships">NCAA Skiing Championships</a>, most recently in 2003,<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup> as well as the 1977 <a href="/wiki/Association_for_Intercollegiate_Athletics_for_Women" title="Association for Intercollegiate Athletics for Women">AIAW</a> National Women's Skiing Championship.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Men.27s_basketball">Men's basketball</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Utah&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Men's basketball">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Utah_Utes_men%27s_basketball" title="Utah Utes men's basketball">Utah Utes men's basketball</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The men's basketball team won the <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">NCAA</a> title in <a href="/wiki/1944_NCAA_Men%27s_Division_I_Basketball_Tournament" title="1944 NCAA Men's Division I Basketball Tournament">1944</a><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/National_Invitation_Tournament" title="National Invitation Tournament">NIT</a> crown in 1947.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Arnie_Ferrin" title="Arnie Ferrin">Arnie Ferrin</a>, the only four-time All-American in Utah basketball history, played for both the 1944 and 1947 teams. He also went on to help the <a href="/wiki/Minneapolis_Lakers" title="Minneapolis Lakers" class="mw-redirect">Minneapolis Lakers</a> win <a href="/wiki/National_Basketball_Association" title="National Basketball Association">NBA</a> Championships in 1949 and 1951.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Wataru_Misaka" title="Wataru Misaka">Wat Misaka</a>, the first person of Asian descent to play in the NBA, also played for Utah during this era.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Utah basketball rose again to national prominence when head coach <a href="/wiki/Rick_Majerus" title="Rick Majerus">Rick Majerus</a> took his team, including guard <a href="/wiki/Andre_Miller" title="Andre Miller">Andre Miller</a>, combo forward <a href="/wiki/Hanno_M%C3%B6tt%C3%B6l%C3%A4" title="Hanno M&ouml;tt&ouml;l&auml;">Hanno M&ouml;tt&ouml;l&auml;</a>, and post player <a href="/wiki/Michael_Doleac" title="Michael Doleac">Michael Doleac</a>, to the NCAA <a href="/wiki/Final_Four" title="Final Four" class="mw-redirect">Final Four</a> in <a href="/wiki/1998_NCAA_Men%27s_Division_I_Basketball_Tournament" title="1998 NCAA Men's Division I Basketball Tournament">1998</a>. After eliminating <a href="/wiki/University_of_North_Carolina_at_Chapel_Hill" title="University of North Carolina at Chapel Hill">North Carolina</a> to advance to the final round, Utah lost the championship game to <a href="/wiki/Kentucky_Wildcats" title="Kentucky Wildcats">Kentucky</a>, 78?69.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Football">Football</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Utah&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Football">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Utah_Utes_football" title="Utah Utes football">Utah Utes football</a>
     </div> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:UtesRiceEccles2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/UtesRiceEccles2.jpg/220px-UtesRiceEccles2.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/UtesRiceEccles2.jpg/330px-UtesRiceEccles2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/UtesRiceEccles2.jpg/440px-UtesRiceEccles2.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:UtesRiceEccles2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Rice%E2%80%93Eccles_Stadium" title="Rice?Eccles Stadium" class="mw-redirect">Rice?Eccles Stadium</a> during a football game
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>In 2004?2005, the football team, coached by <a href="/wiki/Urban_Meyer" title="Urban Meyer">Urban Meyer</a> and quarterbacked by <a href="/wiki/Alex_Smith" title="Alex Smith">Alex Smith</a>, along with defensive great <a href="/wiki/Eric_Weddle" title="Eric Weddle">Eric Weddle</a>, went 11?0 during the regular season and defeated <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pittsburgh" title="University of Pittsburgh">Pittsburgh</a> 35?7 in the <a href="/wiki/2005_Fiesta_Bowl" title="2005 Fiesta Bowl">2005 Fiesta Bowl</a>, becoming the first team from a conference without an automatic <a href="/wiki/Bowl_Championship_Series" title="Bowl Championship Series">Bowl Championship Series</a> (BCS) bid to go to a BCS bowl game.<sup id="cite_ref-fiesta_bowl_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fiesta_bowl-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> The team ended its perfect 12?0 season ranked 4th in AP polling.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>2008?2009 was another undefeated year for the football team, coached by <a href="/wiki/Kyle_Whittingham" title="Kyle Whittingham">Kyle Whittingham</a>, as they finished the season 13?0 and defeated Alabama 31?17 in the <a href="/wiki/2009_Sugar_Bowl" title="2009 Sugar Bowl">2009 Sugar Bowl</a>. Utah finished the season 2nd in AP polling, their highest rank ever. At the end of the season, the Utes were the only unbeaten team in the country, with the nation's longest active streak of bowl victories (8).<sup id="cite_ref-sugar_bowl_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sugar_bowl-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The Utah Utes moved to the Pac-12 Conference for the start of the 2011?2012 football season. They are in the South Division with <a href="/wiki/University_of_Colorado_at_Boulder" title="University of Colorado at Boulder" class="mw-redirect">University of Colorado</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Arizona" title="University of Arizona">University of Arizona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arizona_State_University" title="Arizona State University">Arizona State University</a>, <a href="/wiki/UCLA" title="UCLA" class="mw-redirect">UCLA</a> and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Southern_California" title="University of Southern California">University of Southern California</a>. Their first game in the Pac-12 was at <a href="/wiki/University_of_Southern_California" title="University of Southern California">USC</a> on September 10, 2011, and resulted in a 23?14 Utah loss.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Gymnastics">Gymnastics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Utah&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Gymnastics">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/Utah_Red_Rocks" title="Utah Red Rocks">Utah Red Rocks</a>
     </div> 
     <p>The women's gymnastics team, coached by Greg Marsden, the <a href="/wiki/Utah_Red_Rocks" title="Utah Red Rocks">Red Rocks</a>, has won ten national championships, including the 1981 <a href="/wiki/Association_for_Intercollegiate_Athletics_for_Women" title="Association for Intercollegiate Athletics for Women">AIAW</a> championship, and placed 2nd nationally eight times. As of 2013, it has qualified for the <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Women%27s_Gymnastics_championship" title="NCAA Women's Gymnastics championship" class="mw-redirect">NCAA championship</a> every year since 1976, the only program to do so. The program has averaged over 11,000 fans per meet 1992?2010 and has been the NCAA gymnastics season attendance champions 16 of these 19 years. In 2010, there was an average of 14,213 fans per meet, the largest crowd being 15,030.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Marching_band">Marching band</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Utah&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Marching band">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The university <a href="/wiki/Marching_band" title="Marching band">marching band</a>, known as the &quot;Pride of Utah&quot;,<sup id="cite_ref-official_band_page_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-official_band_page-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup> perform at all home football games, as well as some away games and bowl games. They performed at the <a href="/wiki/2005_Fiesta_Bowl" title="2005 Fiesta Bowl">2005 BCS Tostitos Fiesta Bowl</a>, the <a href="/wiki/2009_Sugar_Bowl" title="2009 Sugar Bowl">2009 BCS Allstate Sugar Bowl</a>, and the Inaugural Parade of President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-official_band_page_98-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-official_band_page-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The band began as a military band in the 1940s. In 1948, university president <a href="/wiki/A._Ray_Olpin" title="A. Ray Olpin">A. Ray Olpin</a> recruited Ron Gregory from <a href="/wiki/Ohio_State_University" title="Ohio State University">Ohio State University</a> to form a collegiate marching band. Support for the band dwindled in the 60s, and ASUU (the Associated Students of the University of Utah) discontinued its funding in 1969.<sup id="cite_ref-ute_traditions_10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ute_traditions-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> The band was revived in 1976 after a fund raising effort.<sup id="cite_ref-ute_traditions_10-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ute_traditions-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> under the direction of Gregg I. Hanson<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup> As of 2011, the band is under the direction of Dr. Brian Sproul.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_life">Student life</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Utah&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Student life">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Uofu_union.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Uofu_union.jpg/220px-Uofu_union.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Uofu_union.jpg/330px-Uofu_union.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Uofu_union.jpg/440px-Uofu_union.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Uofu_union.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/A._Ray_Olpin" title="A. Ray Olpin">A. Ray Olpin</a> University Union and courtyard
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>A large portion of university students live off-campus, as the university is located in a large <a href="/wiki/Salt_Lake_City,_Utah_MSA" title="Salt Lake City, Utah MSA" class="mw-redirect">metropolitan area</a> and has beds for less than 10% of its undergraduate population in <a href="/wiki/Dormitory" title="Dormitory">residence halls</a> and single student apartments. An additional 1,115 family apartments are available to students, staff, and faculty. One of the university's primary four goals for long-term campus growth is to increase student engagement through the addition of on-campus housing, intramural fields, athletic centers, and a new <a href="/wiki/Student_activity_center" title="Student activity center">student activity center</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-plan_elements_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-plan_elements-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The current student activity center, the <a href="/wiki/A._Ray_Olpin" title="A. Ray Olpin">A. Ray Olpin</a> University Union, is a common gathering place for university-wide events such as Crimson Nights, roughly monthly student activity nights; PlazaFest, a fair for campus groups at the start of the school year; and the Grand Kerfuffle, a concert at the end of the school year. The building includes a cafeteria, computer lab, recreational facilities, and a ballroom for special events. The Union also houses the <a href="/wiki/Lowell_L._Bennion" title="Lowell L. Bennion">Lowell Bennion</a> Community Service Center and ASUU (the Associated Students of the University of Utah), which is responsible for appropriating funds to student groups and organizations on campus.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup> ASUU holds <a href="/wiki/Primary_election" title="Primary election">primary</a> and general elections each year for student representatives, typically with 10?15% of the student population voting.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Due to the large number of <a href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints" title="The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">LDS Church</a> members at the university, there is an LDS <a href="/wiki/Institute_of_Religion" title="Institute of Religion">Institute of Religion</a> building directly on campus, as well as several LDS student groups and 46 campus <a href="/wiki/Ward_(LDS_Church)" title="Ward (LDS Church)">wards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup> Approximately 650 students are part of 6 <a href="/wiki/Fraternities_and_sororities_in_North_America" title="Fraternities and sororities in North America">sororities</a> and 8 <a href="/wiki/Fraternities_and_sororities_in_North_America" title="Fraternities and sororities in North America">fraternities</a> at the university, most of which have chapter houses on &quot;Greek Row&quot; just off campus.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The University of Utah has a <a href="/wiki/Dry_campus" title="Dry campus">dry campus</a>, meaning that alcohol is banned on campus.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2004, <a href="/wiki/Utah" title="Utah">Utah</a> became the first state with a law expressly permitting <a href="/wiki/Concealed_carry_in_the_United_States" title="Concealed carry in the United States">concealed weapons</a> on public university campuses.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup> The University of Utah tried to uphold its gun ban but the <a href="/wiki/Utah_Supreme_Court" title="Utah Supreme Court">Utah Supreme Court</a> rejected the ban in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Utah&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:EBC_northeast.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/EBC_northeast.JPG/220px-EBC_northeast.JPG" width="220" height="116" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/EBC_northeast.JPG/330px-EBC_northeast.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/EBC_northeast.JPG/440px-EBC_northeast.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:EBC_northeast.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf9/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Eccles_Broadcast_Center" title="Eccles Broadcast Center">Eccles Broadcast Center</a> is home to three broadcast stations
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The university has several public broadcasting affiliations, many of which utilize the <a href="/wiki/Eccles_Broadcast_Center" title="Eccles Broadcast Center">Eccles Broadcast Center</a>. These stations include <a href="/wiki/KUED" title="KUED">KUED</a> channel&nbsp;7, a <a href="/wiki/Public_Broadcasting_Service" title="Public Broadcasting Service" class="mw-redirect">PBS</a> member station<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup> and producer of local documentaries; <a href="/wiki/KUEN" title="KUEN">KUEN</a> channel&nbsp;9, an educational station for teachers and students from the <a href="/wiki/Utah_Education_Network" title="Utah Education Network">Utah Education Network</a>; <a href="/wiki/KUER-FM" title="KUER-FM">KUER</a> 90.1&nbsp;<a href="/wiki/FM_radio" title="FM radio" class="mw-redirect">FM</a>, a public radio affiliate of <a href="/wiki/National_Public_Radio" title="National Public Radio" class="mw-redirect">National Public Radio</a>, <a href="/wiki/American_Public_Media" title="American Public Media">American Public Media</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Public_Radio_International" title="Public Radio International">Public Radio International</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/K-UTE" title="K-UTE">K-UTE</a> 1620</p> 
     <p><i>NewsBreak</i> is the student-run television newscast on campus.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup> During 2011, program will celebrate its 40th year.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup> Broadcasts air every Thursday night at 10&nbsp;pm during the fall and spring semesters on <a href="/wiki/KUEN" title="KUEN">KUEN</a>.</p> 
     <p><i>The Daily Utah Chronicle</i>, also referred to as the <i>Chrony</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-chrony_press_release_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chrony_press_release-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup> has been the university's independent, student-run paper since 1890.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup> It publishes daily on school days during fall and spring semesters and weekly during summer semester.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup> The paper typically runs between eight and twelve pages, with longer editions for weekend game guides. The paper converted to a <a href="/wiki/Broadsheet" title="Broadsheet">broadsheet</a> format in 2003 when the <a href="/wiki/Newspaper_Agency_Corporation" title="Newspaper Agency Corporation">Newspaper Agency Corporation</a> began printing it.<sup id="cite_ref-chrony_press_release_113-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chrony_press_release-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Society_of_Professional_Journalists" title="Society of Professional Journalists">Society of Professional Journalists</a> selected the newspaper as one of three finalists for best all-around daily student newspaper in the nation in both 2007 and 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup> Staff from the <i>Chronicle</i> feed into Utah journalism circles, some of them rising to considerable prominence, such as former editor Matt Canham, whose work with <i><a href="/wiki/The_Salt_Lake_Tribune" title="The Salt Lake Tribune">The Salt Lake Tribune</a></i> earned him the Don Baker Investigative Reporting Award from the Utah Chapter of the <a href="/wiki/Society_of_Professional_Journalists" title="Society of Professional Journalists">Society of Professional Journalists</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Utah_Press" title="University of Utah Press">University of Utah Press</a>, the oldest press in Utah and now part of the <a href="/wiki/J._Willard_Marriott_Library" title="J. Willard Marriott Library">J. Willard Marriott Library</a>, publishes books on topics including the outdoors, <a href="/wiki/Anthropology" title="Anthropology">anthropology</a> and <a href="/wiki/Archaeology" title="Archaeology">archaeology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Linguistics" title="Linguistics">linguistics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Creative_nonfiction" title="Creative nonfiction">creative nonfiction</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mesoamerica" title="Mesoamerica">Mesoamerica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Native_American_studies" title="Native American studies">Native American studies</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Utah" title="Utah">Utah</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mormon" title="Mormon" class="mw-redirect">Mormon</a>, and Western history.<sup id="cite_ref-media_in_fact_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-media_in_fact-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup> The university is also home to a national literary journal, <i><a href="/wiki/Quarterly_West" title="Quarterly West">Quarterly West</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_alumni_and_faculty">Notable alumni and faculty</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Utah&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Notable alumni and faculty">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_University_of_Utah_people" title="List of University of Utah people">List of University of Utah people</a>
     </div> 
     <p>Notable alumni include politicians <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Anderson" title="Rocky Anderson">Rocky Anderson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Foster_Bennett" title="Robert Foster Bennett" class="mw-redirect">Bob Bennett</a>, <a href="/wiki/E._Jake_Garn" title="E. Jake Garn" class="mw-redirect">E. Jake Garn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jon_Huntsman,_Jr." title="Jon Huntsman, Jr.">Jon Huntsman, Jr.</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frank_E._Moss" title="Frank E. Moss" class="mw-redirect">Frank E. Moss</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Karl_Rove" title="Karl Rove">Karl Rove</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup> recent <a href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints" title="The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">LDS Church</a> presidents <a href="/wiki/Gordon_B._Hinckley" title="Gordon B. Hinckley">Gordon B. Hinckley</a><sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Thomas_S._Monson" title="Thomas S. Monson">Thomas S. Monson</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup> authors <a href="/wiki/Orson_Scott_Card" title="Orson Scott Card">Orson Scott Card</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Covey" title="Stephen Covey">Stephen Covey</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wallace_Stegner" title="Wallace Stegner">Wallace Stegner</a>; <a href="/wiki/R_Adams_Cowley" title="R Adams Cowley">R Adams Cowley</a>, <a href="/wiki/William_DeVries" title="William DeVries">William DeVries</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russell_M._Nelson" title="Russell M. Nelson">Russell M. Nelson</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-nelson_bio_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nelson_bio-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Robert_Jarvik" title="Robert Jarvik">Robert Jarvik</a> in medicine; historian <a href="/wiki/Richard_Foltz" title="Richard Foltz">Richard Foltz</a>; and educator <a href="/wiki/Gordon_Gee" title="Gordon Gee" class="mw-redirect">Gordon Gee</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Notable science and engineering alumni include <a href="/wiki/Jim_Blinn" title="Jim Blinn">Jim Blinn</a>; <a href="/wiki/James_H._Clark" title="James H. Clark">Jim Clark</a>, founder of <a href="/wiki/Silicon_Graphics" title="Silicon Graphics">Silicon Graphics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Netscape_Communications_Corporation" title="Netscape Communications Corporation" class="mw-redirect">Netscape Communications Corporation</a>, <a href="/wiki/MyCFO" title="MyCFO" class="mw-redirect">myCFO</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Healtheon" title="Healtheon">Healtheon</a>; <a href="/wiki/Henri_Gouraud_(computer_scientist)" title="Henri Gouraud (computer scientist)">Henri Gouraud</a>; <a href="/wiki/John_Call_Cook" title="John Call Cook">John C. Cook</a> who played a crucial role in establishing the field of ground-penetrating radar;<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Hartley" title="Ralph Hartley">Ralph Hartley</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Alan_Kay" title="Alan Kay">Alan Kay</a>; <a href="/wiki/Simon_Ramo" title="Simon Ramo">Simon Ramo</a>; and <a href="/wiki/John_Warnock" title="John Warnock">John Warnock</a>, co-founder of <a href="/wiki/Adobe_Systems" title="Adobe Systems">Adobe Systems</a>.</p> 
     <p>Notable entrepreneurs and business leaders alumni include <a href="/wiki/Alan_Ashton_(executive)" title="Alan Ashton (executive)">Alan Ashton</a>, co-founder of <a href="/wiki/WordPerfect" title="WordPerfect">WordPerfect</a> and <a href="/wiki/Thanksgiving_Point" title="Thanksgiving Point">Thanksgiving Point</a>; <a href="/wiki/Nolan_Bushnell" title="Nolan Bushnell">Nolan Bushnell</a>, founder of <a href="/wiki/Atari" title="Atari">Atari</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chuck_E._Cheese" title="Chuck E. Cheese" class="mw-redirect">Chuck E. Cheese</a>; <a href="/wiki/Edwin_Catmull" title="Edwin Catmull">Ed Catmull</a>, co-founder of <a href="/wiki/Pixar" title="Pixar">Pixar</a>; <a href="/wiki/J._Willard_Marriott" title="J. Willard Marriott">J. Willard Marriott</a>, founder of <a href="/wiki/Marriott_International" title="Marriott International">Marriott International</a>; <a href="/wiki/Robert_A._%22Bob%22_McDonald" title="Robert A. &quot;Bob&quot; McDonald" class="mw-redirect">Robert A. &quot;Bob&quot; McDonald</a>, CEO of <a href="/wiki/Procter_%26_Gamble" title="Procter &amp; Gamble">Procter &amp; Gamble</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/David_Neeleman" title="David Neeleman">David Neeleman</a>, founder of <a href="/wiki/JetBlue" title="JetBlue">JetBlue</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cs_history_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cs_history-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In athletics, notable alumni include baseball player <a href="/wiki/Chris_Shelton" title="Chris Shelton">Chris Shelton</a>; basketball players <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Bogut" title="Andrew Bogut">Andrew Bogut</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andre_Miller" title="Andre Miller">Andre Miller</a> and <a href="/wiki/Keith_Van_Horn" title="Keith Van Horn">Keith Van Horn</a>; football players <a href="/wiki/Jamal_Anderson" title="Jamal Anderson">Jamal Anderson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Dyson" title="Kevin Dyson">Kevin Dyson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alex_Smith" title="Alex Smith">Alex Smith</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Steve_Smith_(American_football,_born_1979)" title="Steve Smith (American football, born 1979)" class="mw-redirect">Steve Smith</a>; and football coach <a href="/wiki/LaVell_Edwards" title="LaVell Edwards">LaVell Edwards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-alumni_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alumni-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Notable faculty in science and engineering include <a href="/wiki/David_C._Evans" title="David C. Evans">David Evans</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Sutherland" title="Ivan Sutherland">Ivan Sutherland</a>, founders of <a href="/wiki/Evans_and_Sutherland" title="Evans and Sutherland" class="mw-redirect">Evans and Sutherland</a>; <a href="/wiki/Henry_Eyring" title="Henry Eyring">Henry Eyring</a>, known for studying <a href="/wiki/Chemical_kinetics" title="Chemical kinetics">chemical reaction rates</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Jacobsen" title="Stephen Jacobsen" class="mw-redirect">Stephen Jacobsen</a>, founder of <a href="/wiki/Sarcos" title="Sarcos">Sarcos</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jind%C5%99ich_Kope%C4%8Dek" title="Jind?ich Kope?ek">Jind?ich Kope?ek</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sung_Wan_Kim" title="Sung Wan Kim">Sung Wan Kim</a>, pioneers of polymeric <a href="/wiki/Drug_delivery" title="Drug delivery">drug delivery</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gene_delivery" title="Gene delivery">gene delivery</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Suhas_Patil" title="Suhas Patil">Suhas Patil</a>, founder of <a href="/wiki/Cirrus_Logic" title="Cirrus Logic">Cirrus Logic</a>; <a href="/wiki/Stanley_Pons" title="Stanley Pons">Stanley Pons</a>, who claimed to have discovered &quot;<a href="/wiki/Cold_fusion" title="Cold fusion">cold fusion</a>&quot; in 1989;<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Venkatraman_Ramakrishnan" title="Venkatraman Ramakrishnan">Venkatraman Ramakrishnan</a>, later co-winner of the 2009 <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Chemistry" title="Nobel Prize in Chemistry">Nobel Prize in Chemistry</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Stockham" title="Thomas Stockham">Thomas Stockham</a>, founder of <a href="/wiki/Soundstream" title="Soundstream">Soundstream</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cs_history_131-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cs_history-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup> In medicine, notable faculty include <a href="/wiki/Mario_Capecchi" title="Mario Capecchi">Mario Capecchi</a>, the co-winner of the 2007 <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize_in_Physiology_or_Medicine" title="Nobel Prize in Physiology or Medicine">Nobel Prize in Physiology or Medicine</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-Nobel_2007_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nobel_2007-138"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Willem_Johan_Kolff" title="Willem Johan Kolff">Willem Johan Kolff</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Russell_M._Nelson" title="Russell M. Nelson">Russell M. Nelson</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-nelson_bio_126-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nelson_bio-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
